Bibliotheca Digbeiana, SIVE CATALOGUS LIBRORUM In variis Linguis Editorum,
Quos post KENELMUM DIGBEIUM eruditiss. Virum possedit Illustrissimus GEORGIUS
Comes BRISTOL. nuper defunctus.

Accedit and alia Bibliotheca non minus Copiosa, and Elegans.

Horum AUCTIO habebitur LONDINI, Apud Insigne Leonis Aurei ex adverso
Oenopolii, cujus Insigne Caput Regine in Platea vulgo dicta Paternoster Row,
Aprilis 19. 1680.

The Catalogue is to be delivered gratis by H. Brom, at the Gun, and B. Took
at the Ship in St. Paul's Churchyard.

TO THE READER.
THis Catalogue consists principally of the Library of the Right Honorable
George late Earl of Bristol, a great part of which were the Curiosities
collected by the learned Sr. Kenelme Digby. Together with the Library of
another Learned person.

The Auction will begin on Monday the 19th day of April, 1680. at the Golden
Lion, over against the Queens Head Tavern in Paternoster Row, punctually at
Nine of the Clock in the Morning, and Two in the Afternoon; and there continue
Daily until all the Books are Sold: wherefore it is Desired that Gentlemen
will appear Precisely at the Hours appointed.

The CONDITIONS are these:

I. That He who Bids most is the Buyer; and if any manifest Difference arise,
which the Company cannot Decide, then the same Book or Books shall be forthwith
Exposed a second time.

II. That all the Books in the Catalogue, not otherwise Expressed (for ought we
know) are Perfect; but if any of them appear to be otherwise before they be
taken away, the Buyer shall have his Choice of Taking or Leaving them.

III. That the Money for the Book or Books Bought, is to be Paid by the Buyer
within One Month after the AUCTION is ended, at the Place where they are Sold:
Where, upon Payment thereof, the Book or Books will be Delivered for the Month
aforesaid: And for Convenience of such Persons as live remote, One Month more
will be allowed for Delivery of the Remainder of the Books: The Place, either
where the Books were Sold, or Benjamin Took's a Bookseller at the Ship in St.
Paul's Churchyard.

We desire all Gentlemen who design to Buy, would take the pains to Inform
themselves of the Condition of these Books before the Auction begins; they
being generally Fair, and a very great Number curiously Bound.

Manuscripti Diversis Voluminibus.
1 GEnealogiae Variae diverse. Regum and Familiarum Illust. ab Adam. in 2 Vol.
Folio. 2 R. Gloveri, alias Somerset Fecialis regii, Observationes aliq. de
Origin, Antiquitate and Differentiis Armorum, sive Insigniorum. Folio. 3 --
Another of the same (with the Arms Colored.) Folio. 4 Observations Historical
and Political Mixed. Folio. 5 Articles exposed to the Earl of Bristol after his
Coming from his Embassage out of Spain in 1623. and his Answers thereunto.
Folio. 6 Diverse passages in the House of Lords between the Duke of Buckingham
and the Earl of Bristol, An. Dom. 1626. as also the Articles exhibited by the
said Earl against the Lord Conway. Folio. 7 A Collection of the whole
proceedings of the Session of Parliament which began the 17th of March 1627.
Folio. 8 A Treatise of the Judicature in Parliament. Folio. 9 A Discourse of
the Besieging, Defending and Relieving of the Town of Bergen op Zoom in the
year 1622. Folio. 10 Several Papers concerning the Earls and Earldom of Oxford.
Folio. 11 A Remonstrance of the Commons in Parliament delivered to the King,
etc. Folio. 12 The Duty of the Principal Officers of his Majesty's Navy jointly
considered. Folio. 13 Actions and Proceedings of Parliament in the Reigns of
Edw. the Third, and Rich. the Second. Folio. 14 Life and Death of William the
Conqueror, by Sir Walter Raleigh, and of King Edward the Sixth, by Sr. John
Hayward. Folio. 15 Last Will and Testament of King Henry the Eighth, of
England, etc. with Speeches in Parliament, Letters of State and other Affairs.
Folio. 16 Treatise of the Immortality of Man's Soul, (very ancient) in Old
English. Folio. 17 Mirror of Ancient Stories; being a Treatise of strange
Examples, (in Old English, and Written upon Vellume.) Folio. 18 Poems,
Paradoxes, etc. on several Subjects. Folio. 19 An Epick Poem; relating the Life
and Death of Sr. John Digby; and many other accidents during the Civil Wars
between the King and Parliament unto 1645. 20 Treatise in English, Historical.
Folio. 22 Excerpta e Diversis Operibus Patrum Latinorum, per. G. Digby. Folio.
23 Excerpta e Diversis Operibus Diversorum Autorum de Theolog. Physica,
Metaphysica, Ethica, Censoria sive Critica. Item de Scenis, Variis Structuris,
Iconibus, Symbolis, Emblematis and Apparatu Arcuum Triumphalium. Folio. 24 The
Principles of Geometry. Folio. 25 Lib. Mathematicus (Lingua Italiana.) Folio.
26 Monarchia di Dante Alighieri tradotta da Marsilio Ficino di Lingua Latina in
Lingua Toscana; Item Tractatus de Numero Atomorum totius Universi, and partium
ejus, etc. Folio. 27 Trattato d'Alchymia d' Ant. d' Oration da Sangallo, (Ling.
Ital.) Folio. 28 Lettere and Discorsi d' Ant. d' Oration da Sangallo (Ling.
Ital.) Folio. 29 Many loose Papers (some in English, some Italian) of
Astrology, Geometry, etc. (most being the Calculation of the Nativities of
Great Persons and others) Tied up in a Leather case. Folio. 30 Jos. Glanvill's
Letter to the Earl of Bristol, with another to a Friend of the Usefulness of
the Universal Character with the Way of Learning it. Quarto. 31 Considerations

33 A Chaplet of Roses gathered in the Garden of Loretto; or, a Poem in praise
of the most Blessed Virgin Mary. Quarto. 34 Prodigus Redivivus: or, the
Prodigal Revived, (in Prose and Verse.) Quarto. 35 Twenty Arguments against the

Philosophical Metals, etc. Quarto. 38 Philosophiae Hermeticae Medulla: Item
Medicina Catholica and aliis Tract. Quarto. 39 Tractatus de Morbis Capitis.
Quarto. 40 Oribasii Sardinii Lib. ad Eunapium de Alimentis, Curationibus, and

Astrology, in English. quarto. 47 Tractatus Astrologicus (Lingua Hispanica.)

diversitat. aspectus) in longitudine and latitudine, etc. quarto. 56 -- Idem
iterum. ibid. 57 A Bundle of several small Manuscripts of diverse subjects (most
